News Headlines

Japanese Troops Launch Large-Scale Offensive and Occupation of Northeast China 80

Invading and Seizing Shenyang, Changchun, Yingkou, and Siping Street

Bombarding Our Barracks with Intense Artillery Fire

Harbin Dispatch: Since the night of the 18th, Japan has been implementing its policy of forcibly seizing Manchuria and Mongolia by force, using several divisions to occupy Shenyang, Siping Street, Changtu, Changchun, and other places, capturing key figures in the Northeast's civil and military institutions, and shooting senior frontier officials. The Jinan Massacre is being re-enacted in the Northeast. From the morning of the 19th until I, a humble writer, drafted this dispatch, news from both South and North Manchuria remains cut off. The 30 million people of Northeast China are entirely reduced to the state of slaves of a conquered nation. The details I have gathered are as follows:

First Attack on the Beida Camp: At 9 PM on the evening of the 18th, the artillery regiment of the Japanese garrison in Shenyang, in the name of its commander, telephoned the Northeast Border Defense Command, claiming that Chinese troops from the Beida Camp were dismantling the Liu Changjiang Railway Bridge and damaging the South Manchuria Railway Line near Wenguantun (30 miles from Shenyang), and that the Japanese army was outraged and would take free action. As the responsible personnel of the Border Defense Command were preparing to respond, the Japanese side cut off the phone line. At 10:30 PM, the 41st and 43rd Regiments of the 2nd Division of the Japanese Army, along with an artillery regiment and a hand-held machine gun squad, totaling over 20,000 troops, launched a fierce attack on the Beida Camp outside Shenyang, surrounding the camp's earthen fortifications. They bombarded it with artillery and strafed it with machine guns. Another detachment threw bombs into the camp. The barracks were struck by artillery fire, and a great fire broke out. The sounds of gunfire and artillery were like a continuous string of pearls. The defending soldiers, numbering less than two battalions, were unprepared and, due to prior orders from their superiors, had no intention of resisting and were attempting to withdraw from the camp. However, the Japanese soldiers surrounded the camp and opened fire head-on, resulting in a pile of corpses. By 12:30 AM, the soldiers who had not escaped surrendered. The Japanese army then occupied the entire camp and used bombs to destroy important machinery in the mortar factory. As the Japanese army wreaked havoc, the sound of artillery was heard both inside and outside the city walls. Residents of nearby villages were awakened from their sleep and fled in terror, carrying children and seeking grandchildren, barefoot and bare-backed. The elderly, women, and children cried out on the road, a scene of utter misery. Leaders of the Northeast Border Defense Command and other important institutions, upon hearing the news, were preparing to convene an emergency meeting when a large contingent of Japanese troops attacked from the West Station, Sujiatun, and other locations at 3:05 AM, first occupying the commercial district, confiscating the firearms of the police at various stations, capturing the police, and forcing them to transport ammunition and carry heavy objects. The artillery regiment used artillery to attack the city, destroying important buildings such as the Drum Tower on the north and south sides of Siping Street, the Governor's Office, and commercial areas. Buildings collapsed, and fires raged, visible for dozens of miles. At 3:50 AM, Japanese troops entered the city, occupying the Northeast Border Defense Commander's Office and other important institutions. All communication facilities, such as telephones and telegraphs, were seized. Therefore, after 3 AM, news from Liaoning and Ning'an was cut off. After occupying the city of Shenyang, the 2nd Division of the Japanese Army established its headquarters in the Border Defense Command. At the same time, the headquarters of the Kwantung Army and the Military Police Headquarters were moved to the commercial district. After 5 AM, the Japanese army began to occupy the arsenal, searching for military police and confiscating firearms. They set up artillery in Mawaluwan in the commercial district, bombarding the city to suppress resistance. The residences of leaders of various institutions were placed under surveillance, and they were placed under house arrest, cutting off communication between key figures. Liaoning has completely fallen into the hands of the Japanese army. At 7 AM this morning, Yingkou was also occupied by the Japanese army, which stationed heavy troops from the army and navy. The 19th and 20th Divisions of the Japanese Army stationed in Korea, upon receiving news of the 2nd Division's occupation of Shenyang, were ordered to advance along the Anfeng Line. At 1 PM on the 19th, its advance unit, the 77th Regiment, arrived at Longshan. The five regiments of the Japanese garrison stationed in Liaoyang, Fushun, and Haicheng also began to move towards Shenyang on the evening of the 19th.

Zang Shiyi and Rong Zhen Captured: Rong Zhen, Chief of Staff of the Northeast Border Defense Commander's Office, and Zang Shiyi, Chairman of the Liaoning Provincial Government, were captured by the Japanese army and imprisoned in the Shenyang Concession. Many other leaders of the Northeast Political Committee, Transportation Committee, and various departments and bureaus were also captured. At 7 PM on the 19th, the Japanese army, with a division and two regiments, a field artillery unit, and a machine gun unit, totaling over 30,000 troops, surrounded the Dadong Camp and the Aviation Department, the airfield, and launched artillery attacks. The Dadong Camp originally housed over 10,000 troops, but due to orders not to resist, they retreated to villages more than ten miles east of the city. The airfield, being at night, could not avoid the attack and had over 30 aircraft destroyed by artillery fire. During the intense Japanese artillery fire, the Dadong Camp and the Aviation Department were completely set ablaze. By the morning of the 20th, the fire had not been extinguished. All the essence of the Northeast over the past decade has been destroyed by fire. At noon on the 19th, General Honjo, commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, along with about thirty key personnel of the headquarters, arrived in Shenyang and established a headquarters in the commercial district. At the same time, he issued a public notice to reassure the people, stating that the incident was entirely caused by the humiliation of the Japanese national character by Chinese ambitious warlords and had nothing to do with the general public. He urged everyone to continue their business as usual and threatened to arrest and execute those who spread rumors. He also ordered the garrison to be stationed in various military districts, with the machine gun squad and the entire 2nd Division stationed in the city and the commercial district. The Haicheng garrison brigade and the artillery regiment were stationed in the Beida Camp, the 29th Regiment was stationed in the Dadong Camp, and the 16th Regiment was stationed in the Aviation Department. A 30-mile radius around the city was designated as a restricted area, extending from Wenguantun in the north to Huanggu Village in the west, Sujiatun in the south, and Suanlihong Village in the east. Trenches were dug, and sandbags and barbed wire were piled up in the city and the commercial district, prohibiting entry and exit. The 390,000 residents of Shenyang were all silenced like cicadas in winter, hiding indoors, afraid to go out, fearing massacre by the Japanese army and Japanese ruffians. Siping Street, between Changchun and Liaoning, where a part of Zhang Haipeng's brigade of the Liaoning Army was stationed, was also disarmed by the Japanese army on the morning of the 19th. Siping Street and the area along the Sitol Road were also seized by the Japanese army. The Jinzhou telegraph lines were cut by the Japanese army, and fifty miles of the Beining Road between Huanggu Village and Xinmin was destroyed. Therefore, communication in the Northeast has lost its flexibility.

The Ferocity of the Japanese Attack on Changchun: At 5:10 AM on the 19th, the Japanese garrison in Changchun and the 2nd Battalion of the Gongzhuling garrison, the two regiments of infantry of the Taniguchi Brigade, and an artillery unit were divided into two groups and launched a fierce attack on the artillery battalion of Li Guilin's 8th Brigade of the Jilin Army in Nanling, Changchun, and the two infantry battalions in Kuanchengzi. Battalion Commander Fu of the artillery battalion risked his life to question the Japanese army but was arrested and shot by the Japanese army. The soldiers were furious and resisted from the fortifications. From morning to evening, the Japanese army continuously attacked with fierce artillery fire. Of our 300 soldiers, almost four-fifths of the entire battalion were killed. The survivors lost their ability to resist and were disarmed. The Japanese army then burned 200 barracks and grain stores. At the same time, the three infantry battalions in Kuanchengzi were disarmed without resistance. At 3 PM, the Japanese army presented three conditions to the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office: (1) Release Hao Yongde; (2) Voluntarily surrender police weapons; (3) The Japanese army will maintain order in the city. The Municipal Preparatory Office refused, and the Japanese army used artillery to bombard the city streets. The busiest streets were destroyed by artillery fire, and the fire was intense. The Japanese army also surrounded the Diplomatic Office and the County Government, set fire to them, and abducted Zhou Yuping, the head of the Municipal Affairs Office, Xiu Changyu, the head of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Sun Peichen, the head of the Special Police Department of Kuanchengzi Station, and dragged them into the streets and shot them. County Magistrate Ma Zhongyuan and Lu Qi, head of the County Public Security Bureau, were abducted. After 8 PM, part of the Japanese army moved into Wanbaoshan and destroyed 30 kilometers of the railway between Changchun and Yijianbao. All the Russian railway staff in the two stations of Changchun and Kuanchengzi were abducted, beaten, and looted. Chang Zunyi, the sixth section chief of the railway police, was whipped, his body covered with scars, and forced to provide supplies. Two railway staff members and two switchmen were shot and killed for refusing to allow the Japanese army to confiscate station equipment. The Japanese flag was once hung between Changchun and Kuanchengzi. On the night of the 19th, artillery fire was still faintly heard at Mishazi Station (over a hundred miles from Changchun). All passenger and freight trains between Harbin and Changchun only ran to Yaomen Station (200 miles from Changchun). Telegrams and telephone lines were cut off after 10 PM on the night of the 19th after being taken over by the Japanese army, cutting off news. The Japanese army built a light railway overnight from Changchun to Yijianbao, and the troops seemed to be heading towards Harbin.

Russia Increases Troops Outside Manchuria: It seems that the Japanese military action has the understanding of Soviet Russia. The Japanese Consul in Harbin, Ohashi, is still staying in Boli and has not returned. Kuznetzov, the Russian Vice President of the East China Railway, returned from Dalian early on the 18th, presumably having reached an agreement with the Commander of the Kwantung Army in Dalian. Therefore, in the incident on the 19th, the Japanese soldiers only stopped at Changchun. However, according to a telegram from Manchuria, over 10,000 Soviet Russian troops have arrived at Dawuli outside Manchuria, riding in several train carriages. The locomotives are firing up, appearing to be entering our territory to seize the right to protect the East China Railway. The Headquarters of the Railway Protection Army here has ordered the border troops to pay extra attention and report at any time. Also, Orlov, the Russian Consul in Harbin, visited Zhong Yu, the diplomatic representative, on the 19th, asking him to pay attention to protecting Russian nationals and the traffic of the East China Railway, implying that Russian troops would enter. Today, Matsumoto, a secretary from the Japanese Consulate in Harbin, went to the Diplomatic Office to declare that the Japanese army would never enter Harbin. However, the communication facilities south of Changchun have been taken over by the Japanese army, so the truth can only be based on general reports and the East China Railway's telegrams. The only external communication facility in the Northeast is a radio station in Harbin. The station is a shortwave machine and does not communicate directly with Tianjin, Shanghai. On the evening of the 19th, due to the urgency of the matter, it had to work all night to communicate with Shanghai. On the morning of the 20th, it was able to communicate with Beiping again. Official reports from all parties rely on this only remaining machine, but it can only communicate at 6 PM every day, and news telegrams are squeezed out by official reports. On the evening of the 19th, Orlov, the Russian Consul in Harbin, visited the Japanese Consul and had a long secret talk. On the morning of the 20th, the Japanese army at Changchun Station received a telegram from the Japanese Consul in Harbin, removed the Japanese flag, and only allowed Russian personnel to enter the station to work and repair the damaged tracks. Traffic is expected to resume during the day. On the evening of the 19th, the Harbin Chief Executive's Office convened a meeting attended by the leaders of various institutions, deciding on measures to protect the city and its foreign residents. The Chief Executive's Office immediately issued the following instructions: "It has been reported since the morning of the 19th that Japanese troops are taking free action in Liaoning, Changchun, and other places. Communication facilities have been destroyed, and news is cut off, making the truth unclear. This port is a mixed settlement of Chinese and foreigners and is an international market. Local security is of great importance. Therefore, this office convened a meeting today with various institutions and chambers of commerce to discuss ways to maintain security. Coincidentally, the Changchun Telegraph Bureau and the Harbin Telephone Bureau sent a telegram, which Director Xu read to the audience. The telegram stated that in the Changchun Incident, our army, except for two battalion commanders who died and the artillery regiment which retreated to Xinlizhi, 40 miles from Changchun, all military and police agencies have been disarmed. Changchun is still maintained by the Public Security Bureau and is still peaceful. Post-incident arrangements are being negotiated. Therefore, the situation in Changchun is tending towards peace, and all matters should gradually be resolved through negotiation. The rumors circulating outside are mostly untrue. After this meeting, the military and police agencies will be fully responsible for maintaining order in this port. All merchants and residents must maintain their businesses and not lightly believe rumors or cause disturbances that damage the financial system. In addition to separate instructions, this order is hereby issued to the Chamber of Commerce to immediately notify all merchants to comply. Chief Executive Zhang Jinghui." (20th)

Shenyang Has Become a Dead City 81

British and American Businesses Have Japanese Military Revoke Restrictions

Chinese Bankers Are Negotiating Business Opening Matters

Shenyang Residents Fleeing Have Exceeded 100,000

Demei Evening News, Shenyang, 25th: Several British and American businesses here have jointly petitioned the Japanese military authorities today to allow merchants and residents to resume business. The signatories include Citibank, HSBC, British American Tobacco Company, Arnhold Trading Company, Jardine Matheson, Ewo Trading Company, Asiatic Petroleum Company, and others. Their intention is to request the Japanese military commander to lift various restrictions so that large Chinese banks can open for business. With the closure of large Chinese banks, domestic and foreign trade has completely stopped. Yesterday, Zhang Jia'ao, President of the Bank of China, arrived here from Shanghai to negotiate this matter with the Japanese, but the outcome is unknown. Currently, Shenyang can be said to be a dead city in terms of business, except for retailers of food and daily necessities. The only activity seen today is the movement of Japanese troops and the departure of refugees from the city. Shenyang has a population of 400,000, and according to today's statistics, those who have fled to other places have exceeded 100,000. The streets are filled with various vehicles loaded with furniture and luggage, leaving the city in an endless stream. Chinese officials and police have long since fled, and there is not a single person who can negotiate with the Japanese.

The Fall of Changchun 82

Japanese Troops Launch Surprise Attack at Dawn

Over 1,000 Innocent Chinese Soldiers and Civilians Killed or Wounded

Changchun Dispatch: Various groups of the South Manchuria Japanese Autonomous League held repeated meetings, actively advocating using the Nakamura Incident as a pretext to exert pressure by force and implement the occupation of Manchuria. They repeatedly telegraphed for troops, unable to wait. The result of the meetings of Japanese officials and civilians in Changchun was that they strongly advocated that the issue must be resolved by force. As a result, on the 18th and 19th, Liaoning and Changchun were completely occupied by the Japanese army. The following is an investigation into the Japanese army's pre-attack preparations and the attack itself:

Japanese Army's Pre-Attack Preparations: Kanakawa Nakazo, commander of the 3rd Brigade of the Japanese Army stationed in Changchun, and Brigade Commander Taniguchi Terugo believed that since the Japanese military in Shenyang had already launched an attack, the Japanese military in Changchun should also respond simultaneously. Therefore, on the afternoon of the 18th, at 4-5 PM, they distributed pamphlets calling up reservists to assemble and await orders, but our side was unaware. At 9-10 PM, they used city buses to secretly transport Japanese residents and property to the concession, with a dozen or so buses shuttling back and forth, but our side did not notice. Around midnight, to conceal their actions from the Chinese, the Japanese army used a dozen or so fire trucks to secretly transport over 200 large guns and distribute them to Japanese police (Japanese police do not normally carry guns). The rest were distributed to Japanese merchants, and reservists were summoned to await orders to depart. At 12:50 AM, Japanese military police received secret orders from Kanakawa and Taniguchi to deploy troops to guard all areas from the Dongda Bridge to the West Park, from the south to the Park Yashima Bridge, from the north to Erdaogou Sanbuguan, and the South Gouyan area of the Middle East Railway Station, and to deploy ambushes and sentries in the nearby sorghum fields. Armed police were stationed at all key intersections, patrolling and guarding. By 2 AM on the 19th, the military deployment was complete, and at 3:35 AM, the order for a general attack was given. At 4 AM, the artillery roared, and death was everywhere.

Attack on the Erdaogou Barracks: Taniguchi, commander of the 3rd Brigade of the Japanese Army stationed in Changchun, acting on the orders of Commander Kanakawa, at 3:35 AM on the 19th, commanded the brigade's 4th Regiment Commander Oshima and others to lead a detachment of about 350-360 soldiers, carrying 4 machine guns and 2 landing guns, to attack the headquarters of the 3rd Battalion of our Northeast Army in Erdaogou. After the Japanese soldiers arrived, they first set up guns and cannons in front of the camp, and then surrounded our battalion headquarters. Fu Guanjun, commander of the 3rd Battalion of our army, had received a telegram from Commander Xi Dai of the Jilin Border Defense Command on the night of the 18th, stating that if the Japanese army attacked, they should not resist and should retreat completely, awaiting a negotiated settlement. Because of the order, they did not resist. Japanese soldiers first surrounded the 3rd Battalion. A certain Japanese military officer broke into the camp to meet Battalion Commander Fu. Fu asked what he wanted, and the Japanese officer said he wanted to disarm them. Fu replied that they could retreat, but they would not disarm. Unexpectedly, the Japanese military officer suddenly drew a pistol and shot Battalion Commander Fu dead on the spot. At this time, the Japanese army outside the camp opened fire, strafing with machine guns. Japanese soldiers on both sides attacked with rifles, and the ambushes to the south and outside opened fire simultaneously, attacking our Erdaogou Station and the 3rd Battalion headquarters. When the soldiers of our 3rd Battalion saw that Battalion Commander Fu had been shot dead, they began to resist. The Japanese army took advantage of our unpreparedness and the order to retreat, and the 3rd Battalion soldiers were naturally no match. From 4:11 AM, the attack began, and the artillery fire only subsided at 8:22 AM. As a result, all the soldiers of the 3rd Battalion were disarmed. In addition to Battalion Commander Fu being shot dead by the Japanese military officer on the spot, 80-90 soldiers of the 3rd Battalion were killed, 40-50 were wounded, and 260-270 civilians were killed by Japanese artillery fire. On the Japanese side, over 30 were killed and over 10 were wounded. The auditorium of the 7th Middle School of the Special District of the East Province was destroyed by Japanese artillery fire, the roof was blown off, and over 20 student dormitories were also destroyed. Few of the school's buildings remained. 30-40 students were killed, and over 20 were wounded. The Middle East Railway police were all disarmed by the Japanese army. The surviving students of the 7th Middle School were also placed under surveillance and house arrest, and were not allowed to enter or leave. Both telephone and telegraph lines were also cut by the Japanese army, cutting off news. Detailed figures for the dead and wounded could not be verified. However, all military, government, police, and educational institutions in Erdaogou were occupied by the Japanese army, and troops were stationed there to guard them, prohibiting people from passing through. This is the true picture of the Japanese army's attack on Erdaogou.

Occupying the Nanling Barracks: Kanakawa, commander of the 3rd Brigade of the Japanese Army, and Brigade Commander Taniguchi, using the 4th Regiment and the garrison to attack Erdaogou, was as easy as turning over a hand. However, the Jilin army had a large number of troops stationed in Nanling, numbering over two regiments, and they were deeply afraid that their forces were weak and difficult to conquer. Therefore, they telegraphed for part of the Japanese Marine Corps garrison in Fanjatun and Gongzhuling, about 350-360 soldiers, to assist in attacking Nanling. After receiving the order, the troops arrived in Changchun on the 5 AM South Manchuria train. Under the command of Brigade Commander Taniguchi, about 150-160 soldiers from the 4th Regiment and part of the garrison attacked our Nanling Barracks from both sides. Mu Chun Chang, commander of the 19th Artillery Regiment of the Northeast Army in Nanling, and Ren Guodong, commander of the 671st Regiment, had both received orders to retreat. When the Japanese army advanced, they thought it was a live-fire exercise and did not report or prepare. At this time, most of the officers and soldiers were asleep. When the Japanese army opened fire and attacked fiercely, they realized something was wrong, but our army had no time to retreat. At that time, a detachment of the Japanese army, numbering several dozen soldiers, jumped over the rear camp wall and stabbed soldiers with bayonets and short knives, killing everyone they saw and shooting them. As a result, our officers and soldiers were unable to resist, and dozens were killed on the spot. The rest of the troops retreated in the east, west, and south directions. Seeing our troops retreating, the Japanese army used field, mountain, and mortar guns to provide cover for the general attack and strafed and shot with machine guns. Our infantry regiment's guns and cannons were not lost, but the armory had been locked by the clerks, and all the ammunition was stored inside. It was reported that it was destroyed by the Japanese army, and a large number of guns and ammunition were looted. From 5:11 AM on the 19th, the general attack began. During the 6th, 7th, 8th, and 9th hours, as the soldiers of the artillery and infantry regiments of our side were retreating, and as the farmers on Nanling Street were fleeing, the Japanese army's artillery and machine gun fire was extremely fierce. This was the period when our soldiers and civilians suffered the most casualties. Seeing our soldiers retreating, the Japanese army still supervised its troops to pursue, attacking from all sides and intercepting from all directions, shooting everyone they saw, regardless of whether they were soldiers or civilians, without exception. This was the first period when our soldiers and civilians suffered the most casualties. By 11-12 o'clock, all of our soldiers had retreated to the Jichang Station east of the river, the Yujia Oil Mill south of the city, and the Diaojia Yamaguchi area. Only a small number of soldiers remained, and because they had no time to retreat, they were trapped in the camp and resisted with their lives. The Japanese army's artillery and machine guns continued to attack fiercely. The soldiers of our army who were trapped in the camp were all buried in the Japanese artillery fire. The artillery fire gradually subsided until 1:20 PM, and all parts of our Nanling camp were completely occupied. At 2:53 PM, a cavalry detachment of the Japanese army arrived from Datun Xiaozhan to reinforce the front, numbering about 170 soldiers, carrying 4 machine guns and 2 cannons. The artillery fire immediately intensified. In addition to destroying our army's camp headquarters, the cavalry and infantry jointly attacked our ammunition depot. In fact, our soldiers guarding the depot had already withdrawn. The Japanese army knew this, but deliberately used artillery and gunfire to attack. Nearby villagers' houses were destroyed by Japanese artillery, and countless fleeing farmers were killed. This was the third period when our farmers suffered the most casualties. In short, from 5:11 AM to 5:35 PM, the Japanese army's artillery fire completely stopped. Reporters risked their lives to investigate, but were unable to pass because the Japanese army was guarding the pass. Only a general number was obtained. In Nanling, about 250-260 of our soldiers were killed, 30-40 were wounded, and about 170-180 civilians and rural farmers were killed, and over 30 were wounded. At present, all departments of our army's camp in Nanling have been completely occupied by the Japanese army, and troops have been sent to guard them, setting up posts and sentries.

Burning Barracks and Ammunition Depot: When the Japanese army attacked Nanling, they first set fire to the Changchun County military firewood and grass depot and the grain depot, burning over 300,000 bundles of our army's firewood and 250,000-260,000 bundles of straw. Then they attacked the Nanling Barracks, and after occupying them, at around 2 PM, the Japanese army jointly surrounded the ammunition depot. They were deeply afraid that there would be ambushes in the ammunition depot to resist, but they did not know that they had already withdrawn. The Japanese army deliberately attacked with artillery and strafed with machine guns, bombarding for 5-6 hours. In addition to destroying most of the nearby civilian houses, they also burned all the barracks of our infantry and artillery camps and the barracks of the 2nd and 3rd battalions. At 5:20 PM, they also used artillery to bombard and burn our ammunition depot. For a time, the flames soared into the sky, and the explosions of the ammunition were like thunder. Many of our farmers were killed by the Japanese army. Many of the houses of the villagers in Nanling were destroyed by artillery. Our army did not resist, and the Japanese army suffered no more than 10-20 deaths, and the exact number is not known. From 5 AM on the 19th to 9 PM, the sound of gunfire and artillery subsided slightly. Civilian houses and barracks were still engulfed in flames. (Evening of the 19th)

Japanese Army Invades

News from the Northeast after the Incident 83

A Momentary Scare in the City

Consuls of Various Countries Jointly Maintain Order

Tianjin Dispatch: Since the Japanese army violently occupied Shenyang, Jilin, and other places, according to news from here yesterday, the western route has already extended to Xinmin, and the eastern route is still planning to invade Harbin. Military actions are escalating, which is truly an unprecedented disgrace to our country. In recent days, a large number of refugees fleeing from Shenyang have moved west to Pingjin. These people, carrying their sons and daughters, have nothing on them. When asked about their suffering, it is truly hair-raising. Important officials in Shenyang, such as Rong Zhen, Chen Xingya, Lao Mian, Zhu Guangmu, Huang Xiansheng, and Zhang Zhenlu, all escaped in disguise from Shenyang, took trains at Huanggu Tun, and arrived in Tianjin and Ping separately. Governor Zang Shiyi is still under surveillance and is said to be difficult to release for the time being. Telegraph and telephone communications between Pingjin and Shenyang City have been cut off by the Japanese army since the 18th night and have not yet been restored. The railway from Huanggu Tun to Shenyang has been dismantled by the Japanese army. The Beining railway only runs to Huanggu Tun. Yesterday, the army also occupied Xinmin. It is still doubtful whether the train can still run to Huanggu Tun today. The public sentiment here is extremely agitated. Various organizations and schools have established anti-Japanese national salvation associations. However, because the authorities instructed all parties to maintain a calm attitude, they only held meetings for discussion and did not make any extensive displays. The restrictions on the military and police are particularly strict. Those wearing uniforms are not allowed to enter the Japanese concession. The Japanese Tianjin Command and the police department have recently secretly dispatched plainclothes military police detectives to spy on and report on important places in our country, various provincial and municipal government agencies, and are very active. Therefore, our side is also paying close attention to protecting bridges and all transportation, such as electric lights and telephones, to prevent damage by the Japanese. The Japanese army planned to hold field maneuvers at Haiguang Temple yesterday. Deputy Japanese Consul in Tianjin, Goto, verbally notified the city's Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday afternoon. The bureau did not investigate deeply and immediately agreed. When it was reported to Governor Wang Shuchang, he strongly disapproved and criticized them for not asking for instructions in advance and for acting rashly. After the news of the Japanese army's maneuvers spread in the city, the whole city was greatly shaken. At the same time, the Japanese side spread rumors in the city, saying that several Japanese warships, carrying more than 15,000 Japanese soldiers, had arrived at Tanggu and landed, and were about to attack Tianjin. As a result, rumors spread, and within a few hours, the whole city was in a state of terror. Residents in the Chinese area rushed to various concessions by car at night to take refuge, and it continued all night without stopping. The Public Security Bureau was unable to stop it. Governor Wang Shuchang returned to the provincial government from his private residence around 2 a.m. to discuss security measures. He temporarily consulted with the consuls of various countries stationed in Tianjin and jointly notified the Japanese Consulate General, requesting them to inform the Japanese army to stop the maneuvers. The Japanese army then agreed to suspend them. As a result, the people's hearts were slightly stabilized yesterday, and those who had moved to the concessions returned home one after another. Wang Shuchang convened a meeting of provincial and municipal authorities at the provincial government at 5 p.m. yesterday to maintain the city's security. The meeting ended at 7 p.m. The consuls of various countries stationed in Tianjin, in order to thoroughly protect the lives and property of overseas Chinese, also held a meeting at the American Consulate to discuss ways to protect overseas Chinese. As a result, in the name of the consular corps, they notified the Japanese side that they must not engage in acts that would disrupt public order or provoke incidents. They also appointed American Consul Jervey to personally visit the provincial and municipal authorities to discuss effective protection of overseas Chinese in Tianjin and formulated four important measures: (1) When necessary, the armies of various countries will jointly form a maintenance team and station them at train stations and key points to prevent dangerous incidents of intrusion from outside the city. (2) At present, four American warships and one British warship are anchored 20 to 25 miles outside Dagukou. Four more American warships will arrive in Tianjin within a few days. Belgium and Italy will each have one ship coming to Tianjin. When necessary, French warships can arrive in a short period of time, providing mutual protection regardless of borders. (3) In the special district, a large number of overseas Chinese from various countries live together. The American barracks are relatively close, and it has been decided that American soldiers will be responsible for protection when necessary. (4) British warships are anchored outside Qinhuangdao, and a part of the fleet will be dispatched to the Kai Luan mining area to provide protection in the near future. Overall, the situation in Tianjin is such that because there are so many overseas Chinese from various countries, any changes would have a huge international impact. Various countries will do their best to maintain it, and there should be no danger. (September 24)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 84

Schools Perform Entertainment to Help Disaster Relief in the County: Various secondary schools in the county, in view of the floods and disasters in various places and the misery of the people, urgently need relief. Therefore, the schools have jointly organized a four-day entertainment convention in the auditorium of the Public Education Center, starting tonight (the 26th). All ticket proceeds will be used for disaster relief.

Middle School Student in the Province Writes Blood Letter after Cutting Finger, Condemning the Violent Japanese Invasion of Our Country's Eastern Provinces, Disregarding International Law: The anti-Japanese atmosphere in Songjiang is extremely tense. Yesterday, Ruan Zhongzhou, a student at the provincial middle school, secretly cut his finger and wrote a blood letter to warn the public. It was posted on the wall, dripping with fresh blood. Those who saw it were deeply saddened.

Suzhou 85

Editor of Ta Kung Pao Arrested: Ta Kung Pao of Suzhou published news about the Wuxian public rally on the 25th on the 26th. Due to inappropriate wording, the county party headquarters summoned the editor, Ge Defu, yesterday (the 26th). After questioning, Ge Defu was transferred to the Public Security Bureau for temporary detention, and the newspaper was ordered to suspend publication temporarily. A telegram was sent to the provincial party headquarters for instructions. The Suzhou press is trying to rescue him because the newspaper is usually very cautious.

Wuxi 86

Request to Dismiss the County Magistrate Who Suppresses Public Sentiment: The county magistrate of this county, Chen Chuande, has suppressed public sentiment, controlled public opinion, and obstructed the anti-Japanese national salvation movement. Yesterday, the county party headquarters submitted a request to the provincial party headquarters, which was forwarded to the provincial government, to quickly dismiss him and severely punish him. A circular telegram was sent to all counties, unanimously advocating for his dismissal. In addition, the first district party headquarters and the seventh district public assembly held meetings and passed resolutions to issue circular telegrams to denounce him and request the province to dismiss him as punishment.

Five Men and Women Drown while Celebrating the Mid-Autumn Festival: Fengtangjing in the 11th District (Nanyan City) is about 20 miles away from Tangkou Town. The day before yesterday (the 25th) in the afternoon, 24 men and women from the local villages planned to go to Tangkou Town to buy items for celebrating the Mid-Autumn Festival according to the lunar calendar. They hired a small boat to go to town for shopping. By about 5 p.m., they had all finished their purchases and were returning home on the same boat. When they arrived at a place near the bridge, a sudden wind and waves caused the boat to capsize. Fortunately, a fishing boat passed by and tried to rescue them. As a result, 19 men and women were rescued, but one young girl, one young woman, one old woman, and two men could not be rescued. It was truly tragic.

Nantong 87

The Disaster Situation in Xinghua is Tragic: Zhu Liangfu and others, representatives of the Xinghua County Public Group, sent a letter to the Nantong County Magistrate on the 25th, reporting that disaster relief in the county was impossible to start. Now, many relief groups are powerless due to lack of funds. The situation in various places is extremely tragic. Each ox is sold for only three yuan and five jiao, but no one is interested.

The Wu and Yang Bandit Case is Returned for Retrial: In the Pingchao bandit case, the county government and the court had a dispute over the jurisdiction of the trial of the criminals Wu Qinmin and Yang Jinyun. They were then transferred to the provincial military law joint trial office for trial. On the 25th, the provincial office returned the Wu and Yang criminals to the county government for retrial.

Large Quantities of Inferior Goods Transshipped by Post Office from Shanghai to Various Counties in Northern Jiangsu: In the past month, the number of packages has been particularly large. The Nantong Post Office could not transship them in time, and they were piled up like mountains. All of them contained inferior goods. According to postal workers, every time after the economic boycott against Japan, inferior goods are often sent in packages. This year is more than ever before.

Disaster Victims from the Lixiahe Area are Returning Home in Batches: Disaster victims from various counties in the Lixiahe area of ​​northern Jiangsu were previously transported to Nantong by the rescue team. Currently, the first batch of more than 100 disaster victims voluntarily returned home and were sent by the disaster relief association on hired boats.

Police and Militia Jointly Suppress Sea Bandits: Along the coast of Tongruhai, bandit ships have been appearing irregularly recently. Areas such as Lüsi and Juegang have been heavily disturbed. Currently, the water and land police teams and the defense corps of various counties are jointly suppressing them, and the ports are under martial law to prevent the bandits from fleeing.

Clearing Accounts and Investigating Fraud in the Mang Cao Case: Li Baoshen and others involved in the Mang Cao fraud case in Tongyi have been sent to the Finance Department for custody. The Mang Cao string ticket booklets over the years have all been sent to the Finance Department. Because the string surface knots have been torn off, it is necessary to clear the accounts one by one to see if they match the reported amount of silver, so that the truth can be thoroughly investigated. Director Xu has appointed six staff members and borrowed six staff members from the Zhenjiang County Finance Bureau to jointly verify the accounts to thoroughly investigate the matter.

Zhenjiang 88

Court Investigates Fraud in the Jinghang Road Project: Sun Baoqin (i.e., Sun Minwen), the accounting director of the Jinghang Highway Engineering Office of the Construction Department, and others, led a number of employees to secretly engrave seals in a hotel in the city, fabricate reimbursements, and commit fraud. The Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau was ordered to arrest them the day before yesterday, and a total of eleven people were arrested, including Sun Baoqin, Shao Fengqi, Qin Chongzhi, Zhang Qingyuan, Huang Wenzhong, Qin Dingqiu, Zhong Yuqi, Jiang Baoshu, Qin Chucai, Zhang Fangcai, and Sun Gongfu. Director Chen personally interrogated them once and then sent a judicial police chief leading more than ten detectives yesterday afternoon to escort Sun Baoqin and the other eleven people, along with the evidence, to the court. Chief Prosecutor Xu reviewed the files and immediately handed them over to the prosecutor on duty, who opened the first investigation court at 4 p.m. and questioned them one by one. As a result, they were all taken into custody first for further investigation.

Yangzhou 89

The Cattle Bank Robbery Case in Dayi Collection: Cao Geshan, who opened a cattle bank in the Dongdu Land Estate of Dayi, a subordinate county, had previously come to the Yangzhou Hotel for a cattle transport case. The cattle bank was robbed by more than 20 bandits at the hour of Chou (1-3 AM) on the 25th, who entered and stole more than 1,000 packages of cattle and clothing. This (25th) afternoon, the bank's partner came to Yangzhou to report the robbery situation in order to deal with it.

Page 12

Special Report on Educational News

A Call to the Educational Community Regarding Japan's Atrocities (II) by Shu Xincheng 90

First, Work Hard: Yesterday, a middle school teacher came to talk about how excited the students have been recently, not only unable to concentrate on their studies but also displaying disruptive behavior. The more radical ones even want to drop their pens and join the army immediately. This situation is common in all schools and is the reason why China will not perish. However, everyone must know that there must be a method to avenge humiliation. One cannot act recklessly based on temporary emotions. In this time of great disaster, all unnecessary undertakings (such as the National Games) and money (such as luxury spending) should be stopped and saved. However, necessary and legitimate undertakings and legitimate expenditures must not be reduced. We must know that avenging humiliation is a temporary obligation of our citizens in addition to their regular duties. At this time, we must fulfill our responsibilities as citizens and, of course, cannot fail to shoulder this obligation. However, one must never abandon regular responsibilities to focus solely on fulfilling this obligation. If everyone abandons their other duties because they want to fulfill this obligation, the national economy and people's livelihood will immediately become a problem. Therefore, all of us citizens should do our best in our respective jobs in addition to working hard to avenge humiliation. At the same time, while striving to do our best in our respective jobs, we must earnestly seek ways to avenge humiliation. The current duty of students is to study. Therefore, all students should be loyal to their studies from today onwards as the foundation for avenging humiliation. One must never abandon one's duty because of temporary excitement, nor bury oneself in books and ignore national affairs. The slogan "Study without forgetting to save the country, save the country without forgetting to study" for many years should be earnestly guided by the educational community today to become a reality.

Second, Prepare Strength: The reason why Japan dares to invade our country with tyrannical means is because our country's strength is not as good as theirs. To resist them, empty words cannot help. We must have real strength to deal with them. This strength can be divided into three types:

First, Material Resources: After China opened its ports, due to the constraints of unequal treaties and the oppression of international capitalism, production has declined day by day, and its economic strength is far inferior to others. Therefore, the great rivers and mountains of Manchuria cannot be managed by ourselves and are willingly handed over to the Japanese to act as agents for us. At present, we must of course strive to find ways to resist. At the same time, we must also consider the long-term problems of the future. The responsibility of education is not only to seek temporary remedies but also to seek the prosperity of the country. Therefore, I believe that the educational community should pay attention to the following things in the future:

A. Economic Boycott: This is a way to indirectly increase material resources. It is painful to increase material resources in this negative way. However, it is an easy and effective way at present. It is still worthwhile for the educational community to vigorously publicize and earnestly promote it to students and the public.

B. Promote Science: This seems like a distant water that cannot put out a nearby fire, but the increase in material resources now, whether agricultural products, handicrafts, or war supplies, all originate from science. The reason why Japan has its national strength today is also due to science. If our educators had worked hard on this when they started to implement the new education system, the country's wealth would at least be a little thicker than it is now. However, what is it now? I believe that if we made a mistake in the past, we must not make it again in the future. It is still not too late to catch up. We must know that China will not be finished by dealing with this problem alone. After all, it must stand permanently in the world. Therefore, it is necessary to mend the fold after the sheep is lost now.

C. Increase Production Knowledge and Skills: The decline in production in our country is naturally affected by international economic aggression and the constraints of unequal treaties. The emphasis on governing knowledge in education and the lack of attention to the inculcation of production knowledge and the cultivation of production skills are also very important reasons. If we want to resist Japan, domestic production and economy must at least be self-sufficient on weekdays, so that we can tighten up when something happens and use our remaining strength to deal with them. If we can't take care of ourselves on weekdays, we will have no way to deal with things. The educational community should earnestly share the responsibility of increasing production with politicians and industrialists from today onwards. The only purpose of the future education policy should be to increase production. All schools should take labor as a prerequisite and instill production knowledge in the training of production skills. If we continue this policy for decades to increase the country's wealth, we can resist it in practice when we have the opportunity to take revenge. Second, Physical Strength: Our country's people have long been called the "Sick Man of East Asia." Although schools also have so-called physical education subjects, except for a few championship sports, little attention is paid to general physical training. Facilities for national physical education are even more lacking. The height and weight of the Japanese may not be as good as ours on weekdays, but their spirit of enduring hardship, being enterprising, and being promising far exceeds that of our people. If we want to defend ourselves, and peace is hopeless, we cannot but resort to the path of military solution. Although military force includes various facilities in military preparation, it is people who use these facilities. Whether in any aspect of requiring confrontation with Japan, our country must have people with sound physiques. The current school education should pay at least attention to the following matters for physical education:

A. There are three methods of physical training: one is to use various gymnastics to carry out basic training for various parts of the body to cultivate the ability to endure hardship; the second is to use various sports to cultivate the spirit of Bushido in young people; and the third is to implement physical examinations to prevent and correct the injury of young people's bodies. B. Military training: The conscription system will ultimately not exist in the world. If we want to resist foreign aggression, we will ultimately have to implement a conscription system. At present, secondary and above schools have a subject of military training, but it is only regarded as a formality, so there is little effect. In the future, in addition to proceeding earnestly according to the original method, its scope must also be expanded. As for primary schools, the spirit of military management should be adopted in general schools in order to cultivate disciplined citizens.

Two, determining physical standards: all levels of schools should set standards based on the physical strength of the current people and the people of European and American countries. In the future, those whose physical strength fails to meet the standards will not be promoted on weekdays and will not graduate at graduation. Some educators may think that the method of physical strength is a bit too much, but China's soft education, which has not paid attention to physical strength for 30 years, cannot be achieved by this hard method.

Local News

Anti-Japanese Work in the Educational Community 92

Xu Peihuang Convened a Talk with University Presidents Yesterday

Since the Japanese army dispatched troops to invade and occupy the Eastern Provinces, students and faculty of various universities have risen up enthusiastically to express their resistance. Yesterday, Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, specially convened the presidents of various universities in Shanghai to a meeting at the Education Bureau at 3 p.m. yesterday. Zheng Hongnian, President of Jinan University, Pan Gongzhan, Vice President of China Public School, Liu Zhanen, President of Shanghai University, Chu Huiseng, President of the Law School, Li Zhaochen, President of Jiaotong University, Ou Yuanhuai, Vice President of Daxia University, Jin Tongyin, Secretary-General of Fudan University, Cao Huiqun, President of Datong University, Fan Zhengbo, Director of Moral Education of Labor University, Tang Demin, Director of Moral Education of Jinan University, and more than 20 representatives from Zhizhi Middle School, French Political Science School, and other schools attended. Director Xu reported the significance of convening the meeting first, followed by reports from representatives of various schools on the recent situation of patriotic movements of students in their respective schools. Finally, discussions were held on how the authorities of various schools should guide students to make the anti-Japanese national salvation movement effective and orderly. The meeting adjourned at 6 p.m.

The Zhabei Private Elementary School National Salvation Association Established

In view of the recent occupation of the three eastern provinces by Japanese troops and the killing of the people, the private elementary schools in Zhabei specially established the Shanghai Zhabei Private Elementary School Joint Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association at Jingwen School at 7 p.m. yesterday. More than 50 representatives from various schools attended and elected Du Chunsu as chairman. Resolutions were passed: (1) to request the National Government to quickly order the navy, army, and air force to drive the Japanese troops out of the country; (2) to organize a speech team to propagate the cause, and to hold the second representative assembly at 7 p.m. on October 1 to discuss further matters. All schools in Zhabei that have not participated can register at Jingwen School, No. 37 Shunzhen Road, Tianbaoli.

Anti-Japanese Associations of Various Universities Send Telegrams

University Students Around the World Uphold Justice

Yesterday, the cadres of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation of University Students, because the representatives of various schools have gone to Beijing to petition, the students remaining in Shanghai should take concerted action and should have a strict organization. Yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m., they specially convened a temporary emergency cadre meeting at the Youth Propaganda Corps. As a result, it was resolved to send telegrams to university students around the world, asking them to uphold justice on the Japanese issue, and to carry out a number of tasks during the period of school strikes. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Cadres: Xu Sheng and Liu Liangkan of Jiaotong University, Shi Huikang of Tongwen, Ren Xinli of Labor University, Wang Yaodong and Ji Shiyuan of Political Science School, Xue Yigeng of Datong, Liang Peishu, Chen Fuzhen, and Peng of Fudan, Wang Ruinian of Daxia, and Zhu Youhuan of Guanghua.

All representatives of this association are expected to attend.

Shanghai Middle School Students Armed and Departing 93

Since the Shanghai Provincial Middle School of this city implemented strict Boy Scout training for junior high school and military training for senior high school students from the 17th year onwards, the uniforms have been neat, and military discipline has been strict. Recently, after the violent Japanese abruptly invaded our northeastern strongholds, it is heard that the school has further intensified the training of student soldiers, Boy Scouts, and female paramedics. Yesterday, the entire city's populace held a mass meeting at the public sports field. All one thousand students of the school, fully armed, participated in full formation, led by instructors and faculty members, and then disbanded. Later, they re-formed at Xieqiao, Zhaozhou Road, and Fangbang Bridge and paraded through Laoximen, Zhonghua Road, and back to the school. The spectators along the way were greatly encouraged. In the afternoon, the school's male and female students divided into teams and went to various villages in Pudong to give speeches.

Southeast Women's Physical Education School Vows Not to Buy Japanese Goods

After participating in the citywide mass meeting on the morning of the 26th, the Southeast Women's Physical Education School in Jiangwan immediately returned to the school and held a general assembly of all students. There was a three-minute moment of silence. Before it ended, crying was heard in the field, and then all the students cried in each others' arms. It was resolved that: (1) From now on, all faculty and students will no longer purchase Japanese goods, and those found will be expelled from school. (2) The school is requested to intensify Boy Scout and first aid courses in preparation for war. (3) Slogans and firm reports will be posted throughout the school to maintain constant vigilance.

Labor University's Zhang Yuanruo Authors Oath of National Salvation

All faculty and students of Labor University participated in the citywide mass meeting yesterday. Zhang Yuanruo, Dean of the School of Social Sciences of the university, also drafted an "Oath of National Salvation," which was distributed at the meeting, believing that after suffering a severe blow, the entire nation should be determined to engage in permanent struggle to save the country, completely eliminating the usual weakness, frailty, selfishness, harm to the public, laziness, greed, arrogance, cowardice, licentiousness, frivolity, revelry, and foolishness, along with deep-rooted maladies and accumulated malpractices. The oath contains twelve articles: (1) Develop national production. (2) Increase work efficiency. (3) Enrich public knowledge. (4) Emphasize scientific research. (5) Train organizational skills. (6) Cultivate national consciousness. (7) Strengthen the national physique. (8) Intensify military training. (9) Vow not to harm others for personal gain. (10) Vow not to fear difficulties and seek temporary ease. (11) Vow not to be lazy and wasteful. (12) Vow not to purchase or use foreign goods.

University Student Representatives' Actions in Beijing

丨 Attending the Nanjing Academic Community's National Salvation Conference

丨 Jointly Requesting the Government to Send Troops to Punish Japan

Chu Ping'an, Li Chunsun, and other representatives from the Shanghai University Students' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation arrived in Beijing yesterday morning and stayed at the Central University. They immediately attended the Nanjing Academic Community's National Salvation Federation conference. The two sides had very harmonious opinions and decided to work together to save the country. Once the Shanghai student delegation requesting the dispatch of troops arrives in Beijing, they will jointly request the government to declare war on Japan immediately.

West Lake Art Academy's Volunteer Corps Established

The National West Lake Art Academy, secluded in the heart of the lake, has students who mostly prioritize their studies and are cautious in handling matters, as has always been the case. This time, due to the inhumane actions of the Japanese, they roused their usual passion for art and rose up resolutely. On the afternoon of the 24th, they convened all students at the school to organize an anti-Japanese national salvation volunteer corps. About three hundred male and female students from the school immediately joined, with over two hundred and eighty people participating. They also intensified military training in the coming days to prepare for any eventuality.

Jinling University's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association's Work

The capital's Jinling University has suspended classes for three days starting yesterday to engage in the anti-Japanese movement. Faculty, students, and staff have jointly organized the Jinling University Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. Faculty members, under the name of academic organizations, have issued telegrams translated into various languages for international propaganda and exposure, denouncing Japan's barbarity, unreasonableness, and disregard for humanity, justice, and righteousness. Students and staff have organized an anti-Japanese national salvation army. Male students undergo military training every day from 7:30 AM to 11:00 AM. Female students receive nursing training and practice calisthenics. From 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM, they listen to military academic lectures. In the afternoon, the entire group divides into teams to promote propaganda and inspect Japanese goods. At 8:00 PM, the Japanese Studies Society invites famous scholars to lecture on Japanese issues. It is also heard that the school will continue to suspend classes or shorten working hours and unite with the capital's academic community to launch a major anti-Japanese movement.

Joint Conference of Youth Associations of Various Middle Schools

Letter Requesting Youth Associations in Various Regions to Organize Similarly

Publicizing the Crimes of Violent Japan Occupying the Northeast Internationally

The Youth Associations of various middle schools in this city, initiated by the Shanghai University Affiliated Middle School, convened the first representative conference of various school youth associations in the conference room of the Youth Association on Sichuan Road at 2 PM yesterday. The circumstances of the meeting are recorded below:

Attending representatives: Yu Baiyan, Ni Wencan (guidance teacher) from Shanghai University Affiliated Middle School; Jin Changgui, Cai Lixiang (guidance teacher) from Youth Association Middle School; Wang Mingyin from Qingxin Middle School; Liu Jiangang from Mingqiang Middle School; Wang Hezhen, Li Guanyuan (guidance teacher) from Zhongxi Women's School; Sun Fanghong from Zhengfeng Middle School; Zhong Bingmin, He Luzhen (guidance teacher) from Chongde Girls' School; Huang Jiayin, Li Cheng (guidance teacher) from St. John's Affiliated Middle School; Xu Huiying, Zhang Yunqin (guidance teacher) from Qingxin Girls' School; Liang Lezhang, Chen Jicheng (guidance teacher) from Private Shanghai Middle School; Jiang Ruiying, Li Xi (guidance teacher) from Biwen Girls' School; Wang Lubing, Chen Jicheng (guidance teacher) from Shanghai Kindergarten Normal School; Zhang Hanyong from Hudong Middle School, and over fifty other people.

Meeting Circumstances: Yu Baiyan, representing Shanghai University Affiliated Middle School, was mutually elected as chairman, and Jin Changgui, representing Youth Association Middle School, was the recorder. After performing the formalities, the discussion began, guided by teachers from various schools.

Resolutions of Various Cases: (1) Named the "All-City Middle School Youth Association Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation." (2) Issued a declaration. (3) Requested youth associations in middle schools across the country to organize similarly. (4) Sent telegrams internationally publicizing the actual situation of violent Japan's occupation of our Northeast. (5) Drafted an organizational outline to be handled by the Executive Committee. (6) Expenses to be borne separately by each school. (7) Studied various Japanese issues and issued publications when funds were available. (8) The chief representative attending today's joint conference will be named as an executive committee member of this association. The executive committee will discuss the implementation details of the resolutions.

Fudan Faculty and Students to Petition in Beijing Tonight

Faculty and students of Fudan University are participating in the anti-Japanese movement with great enthusiasm. They have already formed a volunteer army, training diligently day and night, vowing to dedicate themselves to the party and the country. Before the National Government announced its policy towards Japan, they had already formed a delegation to petition in Beijing, with over a thousand participants. They gathered in the drill field yesterday morning, with strict formation discipline, and are scheduled to depart tonight.

Tung Wen and Zhonghua Students' Anti-Japanese Sentiment Intensifies

The entire body of Chinese students from Tung Wen College set out to promote propaganda in various large, medium, and small schools the day before yesterday, deeply impressing the danger of Tung Wen College into the minds of the general public. At the citywide mass meeting yesterday morning, the school's representatives reported that Tung Wen College to China is like the East India Company to India. The audience was moved and shouted loudly to reclaim Tung Wen College, with a thunderous sound. Moreover, the representatives from various universities, originally scheduled to depart for Beijing last night to petition, believed that violent Japan's dispatch of troops was increasingly urgent and that the representatives should go to Beijing as soon as possible. With the consent of various universities, the school's representative, Dai Shuguang, departed the night before last to urge the central government to prepare to send troops and declare war on Japan. At the same time, the representative carried a document to be submitted to the Ministry of Education, requesting the Ministry of Education to reclaim Tung Wen College in order to eliminate Japanese threats and safeguard educational rights.

Chih Tze Students' Patriotic Zeal

Since Yang Junlin Yu, a basketball star from Chih Tze College, abandoned his pen for the army, all the students have expressed sympathy. Comrades He Zuochang and Zheng Dingluo have been running around all day, almost forgetting to eat and sleep. The lecture team organized by the university department students of the school goes to the nearby Shuili Village every day to give lectures and propaganda, awakening the villagers' awareness of national crisis significantly. In addition, Jin Peishan, a resident graduate of the school, recently drafted a blood letter to his beloved friend Yang Junlin Yu, saying, "Brother Lin Yu, you have joined the army for the country, a natural duty for a man. This time, I left without saying goodbye, fearing your persuasion and causing you more pain. The enthusiasm of you four brothers is enough to awaken the ambition of today's youth. Today is the Mid-Autumn Festival. The moonlight on Jiangwan Road is bleak. Looking at the scenery, I miss you dearly and recite the line 'I cannot bear to look back upon my homeland in the bright moonlight,' overwhelmed with grief and anger. The autumn wind is strong, please take care of yourself for the sake of the country."

Telegram from Teachers and Staff of Jiangsu Provincial Middle Schools

The Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Teachers and Staff Federation sent an urgent telegram stating: To the Shanghai Shenbao and all newspaper offices for public attention, the atrocities of the Japanese army are increasing day by day, and half of the Northeast has been lost. The shocking news has spread, and the whole country is horrified. All citizens are indignant. "Better to be a shattered jade than an unbroken tile." All of us in the education sector should unite and arm ourselves to ensure the safety of the country and the survival of the nation.

Great China University Professors' Conference Resolves to Resist Japan

All professors of Great China University held a meeting yesterday and resolved on methods to carry out the anti-Japanese campaign. The most important are as follows: (1) Actively guide students to strive for the national salvation movement within the scope of not wasting their studies. (2) Intensify propaganda work outside of class. (3) Conduct propaganda abroad. (4) Faculty and staff should custom-make Zhongshan suits or Western suits from domestic goods to promote them. (5) Send telegrams to Chairman Chiang, the Central Party Headquarters, the Ministry of Education, Deputy Commander Zhang, and important figures in Guangdong, preparing for a forceful resistance to the enemy and not engaging in appeasement and false calm.

Sino-French Institute of Technology Student Enlists

Liu Jun Zhenan, a student at the Sino-French Institute of Technology, usually showed fervent indignation at the difficulties of the times. He especially expressed outrage at Japan's repeated invasions. Hearing that the violent Japanese had invaded the eastern provinces again, he rose up resolutely and said, "Is this not the time to save the country?" Coinciding with the delegation of representatives from various universities to petition in Beijing, Liu Jun resolutely joined them, vowing to abandon his pen for the army.

Anti-Japanese Situation in Various Schools

Jinan University: Yesterday, more than 1,000 male and female students and over 100 school workers from National Jinan University participated in the citywide mass meeting. In front of the school, the propaganda section of the faculty's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, led by Chen Guchuan, displayed a huge, self-painted, tragic map of the Japanese army's forcible occupation of various areas, which was extremely alarming and horrifying. Tomorrow morning at 8:00 AM (Monday), a memorial week will be held, during which Principal Zheng will give an important report and speech on anti-Japanese national salvation. He will also lead all faculty, staff, and students in swearing an oath to the Premier, vowing never to purchase Japanese goods to demonstrate their sincerity.

Jiandong Middle School: The executive committee of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Jianguo Middle School issued a declaration yesterday.

Patriotic Girls' School: All faculty and students of the Patriotic Girls' School, indignant at the unprovoked and outrageous behavior of the violent Japanese and worried about the country's peril, convened a general assembly for anti-Japanese national salvation in the Grand Auditorium at 9:00 AM on the 26th, chaired by Ms. Jiang Weihua. Over 400 faculty and students attended and passed the following resolutions: (1) Students of this school should receive military training and organize a paramedic team. (2) Telegrams should be sent to the government requesting an immediate declaration of war against Japan. (3) Telegrams should be sent to the government requesting a strict ban on the import of Japanese goods. (4) Telegrams should be sent to authorities in both Beijing and Guangdong, urging them to put aside their private grievances and unite against external threats, and to cease direct negotiations with the enemy. (5) All members of the school swear to never buy Japanese goods and to organize a committee to boycott Japanese goods. (6) All school staff and students wear black armbands, until the conclusion of negotiations between China and Japan, as a symbol of national crisis. (7) All staff and students should save money to prepare for disaster relief and to help fund the war effort, with teachers starting at one yuan and students starting at one dime, etc. Executive committee members were to be elected, and Sun Xiangping, Yu Jianhua, Li Tianxing, and others gave speeches in succession.

Fudan Affiliated Middle School: The Affiliated Middle School of Fudan University in Xujiahui has organized an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association and joined the All-City Secondary School Anti-Japanese National Salvation Federation to act in unison. Students of the school organized a propaganda team on the 26th, with enthusiastic participation. The team was divided into twenty groups and sent to promote propaganda both locally and out of town. Students remaining in school are required to undergo four hours of rigorous military training every day. The entire school is intensifying its anti-Japanese work.

City First Stadium Athletic Meet Postponed 96

The City First Public Stadium holds an athletic meet every year on National Day, both to celebrate the Xinhai Revolution and to promote public sports. However, as the violent Japanese occupy our eastern provinces, with the country facing a great crisis, the whole nation is in grief and united in resisting Japan. Although promoting sports is important, morale is low, and few people are participating, as expected. Therefore, the stadium has decided to postpone this year's National Day athletic meet until next year.

Commercial News

Finance 97

After Big Jump in Silver

American Bank Also Rises to 38 Cents

Yesterday, September 26th, happened to be the Mid-Autumn Festival of the Lunar Calendar. Therefore, all foreign banks and money industry associations, etc., followed the usual practice of resting for a day. There were no reports on all foreign exchange finance and other markets. However, a telegram from London (September 25th) said that the market rose initially due to a lack of sellers. It was reported that the silver market sequence was completely in an extraordinary state. It was also said that due to Indian silver companies buying in, the market softened after closing. American silver then turned to soar rapidly, even more so than before, with a tendency to go straight to the clouds, opening an unprecedented great rising trend and discovering a new era in twenty years, a rare change since ancient times. The opening of the (Monday) standard gold market is more ominous than auspicious. Another telegram from New York said that the price of American silver also rose sharply by 1.875 cents, already breaking through the threshold of 30 cents. The spot price is 31 cents, and the British exchange rate against the US dollar fell by 8 cents to 3.80 yuan. There were no telegrams between the US dollar and the British pound, and the British exchange rate against the US dollar rose by one and a half pennies to 2 shillings and 8.5 pence. There were no telegrams between London and Shanghai shillings, and the spot price in Mumbai rose sharply by 3 rupees and 2 annas to 5 annas, totaling 51 rupees and 8 annas. The market situation is very firm, it is said.

London Silver Price Suddenly Shrinks Yesterday 98

Returning to a Small 3 and 1/8 Pence

A Reuters telegram from London on the 26th reported that the price of silver suddenly shrank again. The recent price was 16 pence and 3/8, and the distant price was 16 pence and 9/16, a drop of 3.125 pence compared to the closing price on Friday of the previous day.

Review of Last Week's Securities Market

Securities Prices Had Unprecedented Fluctuations; Both Rises and Falls Were Extremely Severe

Market Conditions Were Very Prosperous, with Transactions Reaching 150 Million

During the past week (from September 21st to 26th), the bond market of the Shanghai Securities Exchange was extremely lively due to the huge fluctuations in prices. Even as the settlement date approached, all parties were actively trading, and the transaction volume broke the highest record of the past. It was found that throughout the week, except for Saturday, which was the Mid-Autumn Festival and the market was closed, and Friday, when this month's futures had stopped trading and November's futures had not yet opened, only October's futures were traded at over 16.6 million. Other days, such as Monday, accounted for 24.7 million, and Wednesday and Thursday each accounted for 33.04 million, while Tuesday even reached a huge 45.9 million yuan. The total transaction volume for the entire week reached 155.01 million yuan, an increase of over 26.7 million yuan compared to the previous week. This was because, in addition to the large-scale trading of unified salt tax, 20 customs duties, etc., the prices of 20 bonds, 19 customs duties, good deeds, disarmament, and demobilization all fell sharply, and transactions also became very active. Among them, the unified tax accounted for 38.56 million yuan, with 19.93 million yuan in September and 18.63 million yuan in October. The salt tax accounted for 25.045 million yuan, with 13.12 million yuan in September and 12.125 million yuan in October. The 20 customs duties accounted for 28.815 million yuan, with 16.845 million yuan in September and 11.97 million yuan in October. Disarmament totaled 11.795 million yuan, 19 customs duties totaled 11.16 million yuan, demobilization totaled 9.44 million yuan, and 19 years totaled 9.055 million yuan. The 6% reorganization totaled 288 million yuan, the 1996 public debt totaled 2.81 million yuan, and the customs treasury bills totaled 1.445 million yuan. However, the spot market was extremely deserted, with only 5,000 yuan traded on Friday, and no transactions at all on Monday through Thursday. As for the price fluctuations of various bonds during the past week, the bond prices all experienced extremely large rises and falls due to the dangerous diplomatic situation and the market's chaotic sentiment. For example, on Monday, as the Japanese soldiers continued to occupy various cities in southern Manchuria, looting, killing, and destroying all our infrastructure at will, the market was greatly shocked, and people were very nervous and unanimously tended to sell, like a surging tide. Various bonds could not withstand the pressure and fell sharply to halt trading as soon as they opened in the morning. Only the October futures of the 1996 and 1919 customs duties and good deeds did not halt trading. After trading was halted, the prices of various bonds fell in the after-hours market. There was a slight rebound on Tuesday, with large purchases made by financial institutions to maintain the market, and profit-taking and short covering were also quite active in the market. At the beginning of the week, the market was still firm, but as the Japanese army occupied Jilin and plundered Yanbian, the bond prices fell sharply and were difficult to reverse. On that day, more than a dozen types of bonds were halted due to continued declines. Moreover, as the settlement date approached, speculators and those unable to take delivery were all trying to get rid of their holdings. Therefore, the decline in this month's futures was particularly large, with a difference of about 3 yuan compared to the next month's futures, reversing the past situation where bond prices were higher in the near term and lower in the distant term. However, if bond prices were allowed to continue to fall without taking measures to maintain them, this would directly affect investors and indirectly affect the financial industry, which would be even more serious. The current settlement issue for September futures will not be easy to safely overcome. The exchange, in view of this situation, consulted with the financial industry and obtained the consent of the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank to allow bond-backed loans and engage in purchases. At the same time, there was news that the diplomatic situation had taken a turn for the better, with the United States sending a note to Japan advising them to withdraw their troops. As a result, market sentiment improved greatly, and buying was very active, causing prices to rise rapidly. Upward halts reached ten types, with fluctuations of 7 or 8 yuan in a single day, and market sentiment was greatly stabilized. The market had greatly eased by Friday, and there were no major price fluctuations. The settlement in the coming week should not have any other problems. Although it is still difficult to predict the future of the market, the dangerous period has passed. It was found that the price fluctuations of each bond during the past week reached about 10 yuan, still a fall of 3 to 4 yuan compared to the previous week. The following is a statistical table of the high and low prices of bonds during the past week (in yuan):
