A Tragic and Enthusiastic Citizens' Meeting to Resist Japan and Save the Country 147

— Ji Ping

After the tyrannical Japan forcibly occupied our Liaoning and Jilin with military force, the people of the whole country unanimously mobilized their sad and angry hearts, determined to resist Japan, and took on the responsibility of saving the country and avenging shame. At this critical moment, everyone rose up, awakened the national spirit, and saved the situation. Everyone believed that the most urgent task at present was to save the country. Our lives and property can be sacrificed. Resisting Japan and saving the country is a matter of justice. In the past five or six days, the people of the whole country have been running around, calling out, and showing a spirit of courage and unity in their policies of resisting aggression and avenging their grievances. It can be seen that the people's hearts are not dead, and the country's affairs can still be accomplished. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, the citizens of Shanghai held a citizens' meeting at the Public Sports Ground. The enthusiasm of the attendees can be said to have broken an unprecedented record. Observing the angry psychology and boiling blood of the crowd, it is even more felt that organized and united strength is great and valuable. The presidium was composed of leaders from all walks of life, totaling as many as seventy-two people. Under the leadership of the presidium, these hundreds of thousands of people maintained such a rigorous order. It is truly rare. Unfortunately, the person in charge of arranging the venue beforehand seemed to be too irresponsible. Even the simple radio broadcasting equipment was not installed. Therefore, how many people could hear the speeches and proposals on the rostrum? The countless crowds far away simply did not know what was being said. Among the many groups, the business community accounted for the majority. The Salvation Volunteer Army of the Postal Workers' Union did not take off their uniforms and were all full of energy, which was very admirable.

In short, in this national crisis, whether we declare war or not, whether justice can be upheld or not, we must strengthen our own strength. There is more than one way to strengthen ourselves. Strive to produce, pay attention to science, read more books and newspapers, and exercise our bodies. But the most important thing is to not buy Japanese goods. I hope that my compatriots will, from today onwards, use domestic goods, reduce consumption, and learn to be a Gandhi who lives a hard-working and simple life.

. There are also local products and minerals from various provinces, among which Guizhou and Shaanxi have the most. Guizhou Province produces minerals such as lead, copper, tin, iron, etc., while Shaanxi has more petroleum. The Shanghai City Pavilion has two rooms, with a Grand Shanghai Pictorial and a model of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau. They are magnificent, as if the ancient palace halls are based on this model. The efforts of construction can be seen in general.

The Road City Exhibition, as the name suggests, should focus on road construction and all kinds of needed goods. Therefore, automobiles and road construction machinery are all listed in the exhibition. Automobiles, in particular, have everything that one could want. Ford, Austin, Chrysler, Dodge, etc., all display their latest models. The beauty of the style and the beauty of the machinery each have their own strengths. Viewers can carefully examine them and easily understand the mechanics of automobiles. At this time of construction, the need for automobiles is the most frequent and cannot be ignored.

There are two points in the meeting that deserve the most attention. One is the petroleum mine produced in Shaanxi, and the other is the domestic heavy-duty automobile produced by the Liaoning Mortar Factory. None of the machinery in the car was made outside the factory. It is the first automobile produced in our country. The other day, engineers from the Dodge and Ford automobile companies in Shanghai carefully analyzed it and said that it was better than imported goods in every way. Unfortunately, the Japanese did not care about international faith and have now occupied our eastern province. The mortar factory was destroyed, and years of hard work were reduced to naught. This is indeed a huge blow. I hope the people of the country will quickly rise up and plan for it. Shaanxi's petroleum production is very large. When construction is completed in the future, automobiles will be used extensively. If we rely solely on importing petroleum, the leakage will be unimaginable. Therefore, it is also one of the most noteworthy points.

Therefore, it is proposed to publish a special issue for saving the country on that day. The content focuses on practical strategies for resisting Japan and saving the country, studying Japan and the Northeast problem, and patriotic songs and anecdotes. It does not focus on empty talk. The length of the articles will still be kept short. Please send your manuscripts as soon as possible, preferably before October 5th. This is the notice.

Rotary Club Narrative

A Husband's Wife (25) 148

— Jiang Hongjiao

Mr. Li has been coming home much earlier recently, but the relationship between the husband and wife is even worse than before. Mrs. Li has repeatedly talked to him, but he always ignores her and often quarrels with the servants. One moment he complains that the food is not good, and the next moment he complains that the water for washing his face is too hot. Mrs. Li is also patient and does not say anything. Recently, he does not care about household expenses at all. Mrs. Li does not ask him for money and only uses her own salary to cover expenses. In the past, she could still talk about her depression with Mr. Chen, but now, because Mrs. Chen is often at home, she rarely goes to Mr. Chen's house to sit and talk to avoid suspicion. During the day, everyone in the office is busy with work, and it is inconvenient to talk much. Usually, they would walk slowly to and from the company, talking and laughing all the way, but now he always hurriedly hires a streetcar instead, making it even more inconvenient to talk. She feels even more melancholy in her heart, feeling that men are ultimately unreliable. Even someone as gentle and sincere as him can change his mind, which really makes people feel heartbroken. But she also thinks: I don't have any deep relationship with him. He is a friend of my husband and has his own wife and children. Now his wife has returned and loves him. He no longer approaches me, which is very good. How can I blame him? If I go to pester him again, it will be my fault. Thinking of this, she only blames her own fate. Her heart is always sad, and she gets thinner day by day.

At this time, Mr. Chen cannot fail to see it and is also sad for her, but he feels powerless. He only rejoices that he has restored the happy life of his family. He does not dare to ask Mrs. Li anything, does not dare to talk to his wife about Mrs. Li, and does not want to advise Mr. Li, but hopes to pull himself out of the controversy.

However, these situations have gradually become known among friends. They all suspect that Mr. Chen is to blame for the discord between Mr. and Mrs. Li. They go out and come in together every day, and their desks are opposite each other. There are only two of them in this office. Since she entered the company to work, the distance between the couple has become even greater, which is enough to prove that Mr. Chen has insulted Mr. Li's reputation and encroached on Mr. Li's rights. Mr. Chen himself did not know these words, but they have been making a lot of noise outside.

One day, Mrs. Chen told Mr. Chen what she had heard and advised him to be more careful.

He thought of asking the manager to fire Mrs. Li, but thinking of Mrs. Li, she is really pitiful, and he cannot bring himself to do it. He thought of resigning himself and finding a job elsewhere so as not to be with Mrs. Li every day, but he could not find a suitable position in a hurry, and his own living situation did not allow him to be idle for even a day. He was really hesitant.

Youth Garden

Cheer Up 149

— Min Yin

It's raining, the raindrops in the sky are gradually getting bigger, the originally gloomy Zhang Jun, glanced away from the geography textbook he was being taught in school, slowly got up to breathe some air, stretched his waist, and looked out the window, the flowers and trees outside the window were originally lively shaking, but now, they have stopped shaking, as if they were also gloomy,

While looking at the sky, looking at the flowers and trees, Zhang Jun's classmate Huang Qiyuan came to the door,

"Mr. Zhang, are you still so leisurely, haven't you read today's newspaper, the Japanese soldiers are gradually opening up to our Beiping area," Huang Jun said to Zhang Jun,

"Yes, I saw it, because of this, I am even more gloomy, in the autumn of national affairs, what mood do we have to study," Zhang Jun replied,

"Listen, Mr. Zhang, there are slogans being shouted outside, probably Wusong universities and middle schools are marching, let's go take a look,"

The air outside the school gate is getting more and more tense, more serious, a very neat team of students is marching solemnly, when Zhang Huang and the others saw this, they had many feelings, thinking of the fear of being a conquered slave, this fear is not easy to forget, it hangs in their hearts every day,

In the sound of the rain, I heard the echo of this pace, even more gloomy, but, in this gloomy pace, I felt that this pace contained a solemn consciousness, an active consciousness, that it was definitely not a passive gloom, a retreating gloom, this gloom contained a bright consciousness,

The rain has not stopped, and the pace of this group of young and handsome students has gradually moved to the east,

"Japan is indeed too insulting to us," Huang Jun said, "Taking advantage of the time of our people's flood, to invade and seize land, it is really a despicable country," Zhang Jun said,

"That can't be blamed on them, this is the reason why our country is not strong, if our country is strong, would they dare to invade us," Huang Jun sighed, "That's really the case, if our country is strong, would they dare to do this," Zhang Jun said,

"Therefore, we young people must actively rise up, move forward, move forward to find our enemies, put life and death out of our minds, Mr. Zhang, isn't it, put life and death out of our minds, and fight the enemy to the death, that's right, but we must also be careful and not do things randomly, and be fooled,"

It was already dinner time, and Zhang Jun followed Huang Jun to eat, and at the dining hall, he heard conversations about 111-like things, some of which were very passionate, Zhang Jun was indeed eating uneasily, the innocent spirit of peacetime was reduced, and his innocent soul was covered with a layer of sorrow, the sorrow wrapped in gloom, he knew that the future of the country was indeed to be shouldered by themselves, and that they would not get brightness in sighs, they needed to prepare themselves, work hard, move forward, do long-term brain training, and physical training, in order to achieve their own wishes, the wishes of the family, the wishes of the entire China,........................... he gradually thought about it, forgetting to eat, a smile appeared on his face, and he involuntarily let out a quiet sound in his mouth: "Cheer up,"

Expansion of the Jiaoda Railway Management College 150

— Quan

The Railway Management College of Jiaotong University is the only place in our country for cultivating scientific management talents. In the first half of the year, the Scientific Management Research Association, established by the Ministry of Industry and other departments, invited Principal Li and Dean Zhong of the college to attend. All the members praised the college's ability to cultivate scientific management talents who are urgently needed. They also requested Li and Zhong to make every effort to expand the college to meet the needs of this time of excessive demand. After Li and Zhong returned to the school, they conducted repeated research and drafted a concrete expansion plan, which was submitted to the school affairs meeting for approval. It was then submitted to the Ministry of Railways for instructions. After receiving the submission, the Ministry of Railways also recognized the importance of scientific management talents. Even though the ministry's funds were tight, it had to make an effort to raise additional funds and approve the expansion. Therefore, the Jiaotong University Railway Management College began a major expansion this summer. The expansion plan will divide the college into four departments: Railway Management, Public Administration, Financial Management, and Industrial Management. Each department will have a quota of twenty students. Furthermore, since it has already been expanded, the name "Railway Management College" is no longer appropriate (because it is not limited to railway management alone). Therefore, it was directly renamed the College of Management. The college pays special attention to applied science in order to live up to the name of scientific management. The entrance exams for those applying to the college require tests in physics, chemistry, and higher mathematics. Those entering Industrial Management and Financial Management must also study calculus, advanced physics, and advanced chemistry. They must have a deep understanding of the industrial field and a solid foundation in advanced statistics so that they can conduct thorough research. The Railway Management department will continue to focus on all railway-related knowledge. Public Administration will focus on Chinese language, official document drafting, political science, and public finance. All departments of the college pay great attention to English and French. Students must continue to study these languages for two years after entering the university as required courses. Subjects such as economics, bookkeeping, accounting, and statistics are equally important for all departments. The completeness of the curriculum, the thoroughness of the facilities, and the seriousness of the professors are comparable to those of the Scientific Management College of the University of Illinois in the United States.

Social News

Aviation in Malaya by Qiu Bin-cun 151

(Continued)

The aircraft, named Abel Tasman, was scheduled to leave Batavia on May 12th, which was the day after the Dutch capital's mail plane arrived in Batavia. It would depart immediately upon arrival to save time. It was scheduled to arrive in Wyndham, Australia, on May 15th, and in Melbourne on May 19th. It would arrive in Sydney on May 20th. It is expected to stop at many places within Australia to load and unload mail. As for the return trip from Australia to the Netherlands, the flight will be faster and with fewer stops. It is expected to take only four days from Sydney to Batavia. The passenger airfare from Batavia to the capital of the Netherlands was originally set at 2,500 Dutch guilders, but has now been reduced to 2,000 Dutch guilders. This 2,000 guilders includes the landing fees at each airport along the way, as well as lodging and meals. In short, people in Batavia who want to travel far to the Dutch capital can arrive safely for only 2,000 guilders. Conversely, people in the Dutch capital who want to come to Batavia also have the same convenience. This is truly good news for the travel industry and a sign of the rapid advancement of transportation.

Aviation Locations in Malaya

A British amateur pilot has made multiple flight records between Britain and Australia. Because of his excellent performance, the British authorities conducted a test flight for British-Australian postal aviation to prepare for the future implementation of airmail delivery. The round-trip route must pass through several places in Malaya. Therefore, the construction of airfields in Malaya is extremely important. The important aviation locations in Malaya are listed below:

(1) Penang Airfield

The construction of the Penang Malai Pai airfield has been under consideration for a long time since it was proposed. Although the government has sent people to conduct surveys, the method of implementation has not yet been determined. Local businessmen are discussing this delay, especially in light of the recent commencement of postal aviation in the Dutch East Indies, which is closely related to the construction of the Penang airfield. Local people doubt whether the government is truly proceeding with the construction of the Malai Pai airfield. As for the government's survey work, the Bureau of Public Works sent people to survey the boundaries in January of this year, and the survey was completed in March. It is estimated that the airfield site is located 11 miles from George Town in Malai Pai, with a total of 30 plots of land, all planted with rice and coconut trees. The designated airfield area is 280 acres, of which 200 acres are privately owned. Therefore, there is no problem in acquiring the land. Last month, the director of the Dutch postal airline visited Penang for a week. According to his published opinion, they plan to choose Penang as the flight landing field for the company in the Malay Peninsula, because that place is more suitable than Bangkok, Medan, and Singapore. The company has no business interest in Bangkok, and Singapore is too far to the Far East. Therefore, if the Penang airfield is completed, they will land in Penang. After arriving on the island, he personally went to the Malai Pai airfield for an inspection, believing that the airfield could be completed in the near future. However, he received reliable information from official sources that the airfield could not be completed in less than two years. The Penang European Chamber of Commerce is paying close attention to this matter and will raise it for discussion at its semi-annual general meeting this month to promote its realization.

(2) Alor Setar Airfield

As for the Alor Setar airfield, it already has a rough scale and does not require much construction and equipment. It is already available for use. (To be continued)
